<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>




<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">




<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt">Kraft Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries
</DIV>

<DIV align="left">
<A name="107"></A>
</DIV>
<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements</DIV>


<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">(Unaudited)</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Note 1. Accounting Policies:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Basis of Presentation:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our interim condensed consolidated financial statements are unaudited. We prepared the condensed
consolidated financial statements following the requirements of the SEC for interim reporting. As
permitted under those rules, a number of footnotes or other financial information that are normally
required by accounting principles generally accepted in the United States of America have been
condensed or omitted. It is management&#146;s opinion that these financial statements include all
normal and recurring adjustments necessary for a fair presentation of our financial position and
operating results. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily
indicative of annual results.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">You should read these statements in conjunction with our consolidated financial statements and
related notes in our Annual Report on <BR>Form 10-K for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In the first quarter of 2007, Altria Group, Inc. (&#147;Altria&#148;) spun off its entire interest (89.0%) in
Kraft on a pro rata basis to Altria stockholders in a tax-free transaction. Effective as of the
close of business on March&nbsp;30, 2007, all Kraft shares owned by Altria were distributed to Altria&#146;s
stockholders, and our separation from Altria was completed (the &#147;Distribution&#148;). Before the
Distribution, Altria converted all of its Class&nbsp;B shares of Kraft common stock into Class&nbsp;A shares
of Kraft common stock. The Distribution ratio was calculated by dividing the number of shares of
Kraft Common Stock held by Altria by the number of Altria shares outstanding on the date of record,
March&nbsp;16, 2007. Based on the calculation, the distribution ratio was 0.692024 shares of Kraft
Common Stock for every share of Altria common stock outstanding. Following the Distribution, we
only have Class&nbsp;A common stock outstanding.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>New Accounting Pronouncements:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In September&nbsp;2006, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (&#147;SFAS&#148;) No.&nbsp;157,
<I>Fair Value Measurements</I>. The provisions are effective for Kraft as of January&nbsp;1, 2008. This
statement defines fair value, establishes a framework for measuring fair value and expands
disclosures about fair value measurements. We are currently evaluating the impact of this
statement on our financial position, results of operations and cash flows.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In February&nbsp;2007, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;159, <I>The Fair Value Option for Financial Assets and
Financial Liabilities &#150; Including an amendment of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;115</I>. The provisions are
effective for Kraft as of January&nbsp;1, 2008. This statement permits entities to choose to measure
many financial instruments and certain other items at fair value and report unrealized gains and
losses on these instruments in earnings. We are currently evaluating the impact of this statement
on our financial position, results of operations and cash flows.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Reclassification:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We reclassified certain prior year statement of earnings amounts, related to minority interest in
earnings, from a separate line item into general corporate expenses within marketing,
administration and research costs to conform with the current year&#146;s presentation. Additionally,
we reclassified certain prior year balance sheet amounts, related to dividends payable, from other
accrued liabilities to a separate line item to conform with the current year&#146;s presentation.
</DIV>


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->7<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Note 2. Asset Impairment, Exit and Implementation Costs:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Restructuring
Program</B></DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In January&nbsp;2004, we announced a three-year restructuring program (the &#147;Restructuring Program&#148;) and,
in January&nbsp;2006, extended it through 2008. The objectives of this program are to leverage our
global scale, realign and lower our cost structure, and optimize capacity. As part of the
Restructuring Program we anticipate:
</DIV>


<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt">
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 10pt">

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="2%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>incurring approximately $3.0&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges reflecting asset disposals,
severance and implementation costs, including approximately $575&nbsp;million in 2007;</TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="2%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>closing up to 40 facilities and eliminating approximately 14,000 positions; and</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="2%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>using cash to pay for approximately $1.9&nbsp;billion of the $3.0&nbsp;billion in charges.</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We have incurred $1.9&nbsp;billion in charges since the inception of the Restructuring Program,
including $245&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the second quarter of 2006, we entered into a seven-year, $1.7&nbsp;billion agreement to receive
information technology services from Electronic Data Systems (&#147;EDS&#148;). On June&nbsp;1, 2006, Kraft began
using EDS&#146;s data centers, and EDS started providing Kraft with web hosting, telecommunications and
IT workplace services. In the second quarter of 2007, we reversed $1&nbsp;million in restructuring
costs because our severance costs were lower than originally anticipated, and we incurred
implementation costs of $19&nbsp;million related to the EDS transition. During the six months ended
June&nbsp;30, 2007, we reversed $8&nbsp;million in restructuring costs because our severance costs were lower
than originally anticipated, and we incurred implementation costs of $34&nbsp;million. These amounts
are included in the total Restructuring Program charges discussed above.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Restructuring Costs:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Under the Restructuring Program, we recorded asset impairment and exit costs of $107&nbsp;million during
the three months and $174&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007. We announced the
closure of two plants during the first six months of 2007, bringing the facility closures we have
announced since the program began to 29. We expect to pay cash for
approximately $122&nbsp;million of
the charges that we incurred during the first six months of 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Restructuring liability activity for the six months ended June 30, 2007 was as follows:

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Severance costs include the cost of benefits received by terminated employees. We expect to
eliminate approximately 10,500 positions in connection with programs announced since 2004. As of
June&nbsp;30, 2007, we had eliminated approximately 9,800 of these positions. Severance charges against
assets primarily relate to incremental pension costs, which reduce prepaid pension assets. Asset
write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by plant closings and related activity. We
incurred other costs related primarily to the renegotiation of supplier contract costs, workforce
reductions associated with the plant closings and the termination of leasing agreements.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Implementation Costs:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We recorded implementation costs associated with the Restructuring Program of $50&nbsp;million during
the three months and $71&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007. These costs include
incremental expenses related to the closure of facilities and the EDS transition discussed above.
Substantially all implementation costs incurred in 2007 will require cash payments. We recorded
these costs on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings as follows:
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Asset
Impairment Charges</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the first quarter of 2007, we sold our hot cereal assets and trademarks for a pre-tax gain
of $12&nbsp;million. We previously incurred an asset impairment charge of $69&nbsp;million in the fourth
quarter of 2006 in connection with this sale. The charge included the write-off of a portion of
the associated goodwill, intangible assets and property, plant and equipment. We recorded the
charge as asset impairment and exit costs on the 2006 consolidated statement of earnings, and no
further charges were incurred in 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the first quarter of 2007, we completed our annual review of goodwill and intangible assets.
No impairments resulted from this review.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Total

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>



<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Note 3. Transactions with Altria Group, Inc.:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On March&nbsp;30, 2007, we entered into a post-spin Transition Services Agreement with Altria&#146;s
subsidiary, Altria Corporate Services, Inc. (&#147;ALCS&#148;). Under the agreement, ALCS is providing
information technology services to Kraft during the EDS transition. In the first quarter of 2007,
ALCS provided pre-spin administrative services to us under a separate
Corporate Services agreement
that expired on March&nbsp;30, 2007. Billings for all services were $4&nbsp;million for the three months and
$23&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On March&nbsp;30, 2007, we entered into an Employee Matters Agreement and a Tax Sharing Agreement with
Altria. The Employee Matters Agreement sets out each company&#146;s obligations for employee transfers,
equity compensation and other employee benefits matters for individuals moving, or who previously
moved between companies. The Tax Sharing Agreement identifies Altria&#146;s and Kraft&#146;s rights,
responsibilities and obligations with respect to our income taxes following the Distribution. It
also places certain restrictions on us, including a 2-year limit on share repurchases of no more
than 20% of our Common Stock outstanding at the time of the Distribution.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At March&nbsp;31, 2007, we had short-term amounts payable to Altria of $449&nbsp;million, including $364
million of accrued dividends, which we paid in April&nbsp;2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In the first quarter 2007, we repurchased 1.4&nbsp;million shares of our Common Stock from Altria at a
cost of $46.5&nbsp;million. We paid $32.085 per share, which was the average of the high and the low
price of Kraft Common Stock as reported on the NYSE on March&nbsp;1, 2007. This repurchase was in
accordance with the Distribution agreement.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Note 4. Acquisitions:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;3, 2007, we announced a binding offer to acquire the global biscuit business of Groupe
Danone S.A. (&#147;Groupe Danone&#148;) for <FONT face="'Times New Roman',times,serif">&#128;</FONT>5.3&nbsp;billion (approximately $7.2&nbsp;billion) in cash. Groupe
Danone&#146;s global biscuit business generated revenues of approximately $2.7&nbsp;billion during 2006. The
transaction is subject to customary closing conditions, including regulatory approval. We expect
the transaction to close by the end of 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In September&nbsp;2006, we acquired the Spanish and Portuguese operations of United Biscuits (&#147;UB&#148;) for
approximately $1.1&nbsp;billion. The non-cash acquisition was financed by our assumption of $541
million of debt issued by the acquired business immediately prior to the acquisition, as well as
$530&nbsp;million of value for the redemption of our outstanding investment in UB, primarily
deep-discount securities. As part of the transaction, we also recovered the rights to all Nabisco
trademarks in the European Union, Eastern Europe, the Middle East and Africa, which UB had held
since 2000. These businesses contributed net revenues of approximately $118&nbsp;million during the
three months and $215&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Note 5. Divestitures:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the second quarter of 2007, we sold sugar confectionery assets in Romania and related
trademarks. During the first quarter of 2007, we sold our hot cereal assets and trademarks. In
aggregate, we received $203&nbsp;million in proceeds, and recorded gains of $20&nbsp;million on these sales.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The aggregate operating results of these divestitures were not material to our financial statements
in any of the periods presented.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Note 6. Stock Plans:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On May&nbsp;3, 2007, our Board of Directors approved a stock option grant to Irene B. Rosenfeld to
recognize her election as our Chairman. Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld received 300,000 stock options under the
2005 Performance Incentive Plan, which vest under varying market and service conditions and expire
ten years after the grant date.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">At Distribution, as described in Note 1, <I>Accounting Policies</I>, Altria stock awards were modified
through the issuance of Kraft stock awards, and accordingly the Altria stock awards were split into
two instruments. Holders of Altria stock options received: 1) a new Kraft option to acquire shares
of Kraft Common Stock; and 2) an adjusted Altria stock option for the same
number of shares of Altria common stock previously held, but with a proportionally reduced exercise
price. For each employee stock option outstanding, the aggregate intrinsic value immediately
before the Distribution was not greater than the aggregate intrinsic value immediately after the
Distribution. Holders of Altria restricted stock or stock rights awarded before January&nbsp;31, 2007,
retained their existing awards and received restricted stock or stock rights in Kraft Common Stock.
Recipients of Altria restricted stock or stock rights awarded on or after January&nbsp;31, 2007, did
not receive Kraft restricted stock or stock rights because Altria announced the Distribution at
that time. We reimbursed Altria $179&nbsp;million for net settlement of the employee stock awards as
detailed below. We determined the fair value of the stock options using the Black-Scholes option
valuation model. We adjusted the fair value of the restricted stock and stock rights by the value
of projected forfeitures.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->11<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Based upon the number of Altria stock awards outstanding at Distribution, we granted stock options

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In January&nbsp;2007, we issued approximately 5.2&nbsp;million shares of restricted stock and stock rights to

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The total intrinsic value of the 3.2&nbsp;million Kraft stock options exercised during the second

options exercised during the first six months of 2007 was $55.8&nbsp;million.
</DIV>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Note 8. Contingencies:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Legal Proceedings: </I>We are defendants in a variety of legal proceedings. Plaintiffs in a few of
those cases seek substantial damages. We cannot predict with certainty the results of these
proceedings. However, we believe that the final outcome of these proceedings will not materially
affect our financial results.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Third-Party Guarantees: </I>We have third-party guarantees because of our acquisition, divestiture and
construction activities. As part of those transactions, we guarantee that third parties will make
contractual payments or achieve performance measures. At June&nbsp;30, 2007, our third-party guarantees
were approximately $27&nbsp;million, of which approximately $7&nbsp;million have no specified expiration
dates. Substantially all of the remainder expire at various times through 2016. We have a
liability of $21&nbsp;million on our condensed consolidated balance sheet at June&nbsp;30, 2007, relating to
these guarantees.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The movement in goodwill and intangible assets from December&nbsp;31, 2006 is as follows:

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Note 11. Segment Reporting:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Kraft manufactures and markets packaged food products, including beverages, cheese, snacks,
convenient meals and various packaged grocery products. We manage and report operating results
through two commercial units, Kraft North America and Kraft International. We manage Kraft North
America&#146;s operations by product category, and its reportable segments are North America Beverages;
North America Cheese &#038; Foodservice; North America Convenient Meals; North America Grocery; and
North America Snacks &#038; Cereals. We manage Kraft International&#146;s operations by geographic location,
and its reportable segments are European Union and Developing Markets (formerly known as Developing
Markets, Oceania &#038; North Asia).
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->14<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>




<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Management uses segment operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources.
Segment operating income excludes unallocated general corporate expenses and amortization of
intangibles. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors
analyze segment performance and trends. We centrally manage interest and other debt expense and
the provision for income taxes. Accordingly, we do not present these items by segment because they
are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. Our assets are
principally located in the U.S. and Europe and are managed geographically.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment data were as follows:
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We recorded asset impairment, exit and implementation costs of $157&nbsp;million during the three months
and $245&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007. Refer to Note 2, <I>Asset Impairment,
Exit and Implementation Costs</I>, for a breakout of charges by segment.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the second quarter of 2007, we sold sugar confectionery assets in Romania and related
trademarks and recorded a pre-tax gain of $8&nbsp;million. We included this gain in the segment
operating income of the Developing Markets segment. During the first quarter of 2007, we sold our
hot cereal assets and trademarks and recorded a pre-tax gain of $12&nbsp;million. We included this gain
in the segment operating income of the North America Snacks &#038; Cereals segment.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Note 12. Financial Instruments:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Kraft is exposed to price risk related to forecasted purchases of certain commodities that we
primarily use as raw materials. Accordingly, we use commodity forward contracts as cash flow
hedges, primarily for coffee, milk, sugar and cocoa. Commodity forward contracts generally qualify
for the normal purchase exception under SFAS No.&nbsp;133 and are, therefore, not subject to its
provisions. We also use commodity futures and options to hedge the price of certain commodities,
including milk, coffee, cocoa, wheat, corn, sugar and soybean oil. The majority of these
derivative instruments are accounted for as effective hedges. We had net long commodity positions
of $461&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2007, and $533&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31, 2006. Net unrealized gains on
commodity positions were approximately $70&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2007, and were insignificant at
December&nbsp;31, 2006. We defer the effective portion of unrealized gains and losses on commodity
futures and option contracts as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses).
We recognize the deferred portion as a component of cost of sales in our consolidated statement of
earnings when the related inventory is sold. Ineffectiveness related to the derivatives that
qualify for hedge accounting under SFAS No.&nbsp;133 was immaterial during the three and six months
ended June&nbsp;30, 2007. For the derivative instruments that did not qualify for hedge accounting
under SFAS No.&nbsp;133, we recognized gains of $10&nbsp;million during the three months and $16&nbsp;million
during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007. As of June&nbsp;30, 2007, we had hedged forecasted commodity
transactions for periods not exceeding the next 18&nbsp;months.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We use various financial instruments to mitigate our exposure to changes in exchange rates from
third-party and intercompany actual and forecasted transactions. These instruments include forward
foreign exchange contracts, foreign currency swaps and foreign currency options. Substantially all
of these derivative instruments are accounted for as effective hedges. Based on the size and
location of our businesses, the primary currencies we are exposed to include the euro, Swiss franc,
British pound and Canadian dollar. We had forward foreign exchange contracts, foreign currency
swaps and foreign exchange options with aggregate notional amounts of $5.7&nbsp;billion at June&nbsp;30,
2007, and $2.6&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2006. Unrealized gains or losses on net foreign currency
positions were immaterial at June&nbsp;30, 2007 and December&nbsp;31, 2006. We defer the effective portion
of unrealized gains and losses associated with forward, swap and option contracts as a component of
accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses)&nbsp;until the underlying hedged transactions are
reported on our consolidated statement of earnings. During the first quarter of 2007, we hedged
currency exposure related to new longer term intercompany loans with foreign subsidiaries. As of
June&nbsp;30, 2007, we had hedged forecasted foreign currency transactions for periods not exceeding the
next 54&nbsp;months.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->16<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Note 13. Benefit Plans:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We sponsor noncontributory defined benefit pension plans covering most U.S. employees. As
appropriate, we provide pension coverage for employees of our non-U.S. subsidiaries through
separate plans. Local statutory requirements govern many of these plans. In addition, our U.S.
and Canadian subsidiaries provide health care and other benefits to most retired employees. Local
government plans generally cover health care benefits for retirees outside the U.S. and Canada.
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>



<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the second quarter of 2007, employees left Kraft under workforce reduction programs,
resulting in settlement losses of $15&nbsp;million for the U.S. plans. In addition, retiring employees
elected lump-sum payments, resulting in settlement losses of $19&nbsp;million in the second quarter of
2007. These costs are included in other expense, above.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><i>Employer
Contributions</i>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We make contributions to our U.S. and non-U.S. pension plans to the extent that they are tax
deductible and do not generate an excise tax liability. During the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007,
we contributed $10&nbsp;million to our U.S. plans and $75&nbsp;million to our non-U.S. plans. We currently
plan to make additional contributions of approximately $6&nbsp;million to our U.S. plans and
approximately $82&nbsp;million to our non-U.S. plans during the remainder of 2007. However, our actual
contributions may be different due to many factors. Those factors include changes in tax and other
benefit laws, pension asset performance that differs significantly from the expected performance,
or significant changes in interest rates.
</DIV>

<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><U><B>Note 14. Income Taxes:</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Kraft accounts for income taxes in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;109, <I>Accounting for Income Taxes</I>.
Prior to the Distribution, Altria included our U.S. accounts in its consolidated federal income tax
return, and we generally computed income taxes on a separate company basis. However, some of our
foreign tax credits, capital losses and other credits could not be used on a separate company
basis. To the extent that Altria used our foreign tax credits and other tax benefits in its
consolidated federal income tax return, we recognized the benefit in the calculation of our
provision for income taxes. We made payments to, or were reimbursed by, Altria for the tax effects
resulting from being included in Altria&#146;s tax return, including current taxes payable and net
changes in tax provisions. As of March&nbsp;31, 2007, we are no longer a member of the Altria
consolidated tax return group and will file our own federal consolidated income tax return. Altria
also previously carried our federal tax contingencies on its balance sheet and reported them in its
financial statements. As a result of the Distribution, Altria transferred our federal tax
contingencies of $375&nbsp;million to our balance sheet and related interest income of $77&nbsp;million at
the end of the first quarter of 2007. During the quarter, Altria paid
us
$305&nbsp;million for the federal tax contingencies held by them,
less the impact of federal reserves reversed due to the adoption of
FASB Interpretation No.&nbsp;48. This amount is reflected within
&#147;other&#148; in the operating activities section of the condensed
consolidated statement of cash flows.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In July&nbsp;2006, the FASB issued FASB Interpretation No.&nbsp;48, <I>Accounting for the Uncertainty in Income
Taxes &#151; an interpretation of FASB Statement No.&nbsp;109 </I>(&#147;FIN 48&#148;). The provisions of FIN 48 became
effective for us as of January&nbsp;1, 2007. FIN 48 clarifies when tax benefits should be recorded in
the financial statements and provides measurement criteria for valuing such benefits. In order for
us to recognize benefits, our tax position must be more-likely-than-not to be sustained upon audit.
The amount we recognize is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than 50
percent likely of being realized upon ultimate settlement. Before the implementation of FIN 48, we
established additional provisions for certain positions that were likely to be challenged even
though we believe that those existing tax positions were fully supportable. The adoption of FIN 48
resulted in an increase to shareholders&#146; equity as of January&nbsp;1, 2007 of $213&nbsp;million and resulted
from:
</DIV>


<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt">
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 10pt">

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="3%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>a $265&nbsp;million decrease in the liability for unrecognized tax benefits, comprised of
$247&nbsp;million in tax and $18&nbsp;million in interest;</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="3%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>a reduction in goodwill of $85&nbsp;million; and</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="3%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>an increase to federal and state deferred tax assets of $33&nbsp;million.</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As of January&nbsp;1, 2007, after the implementation of FIN 48, our unrecognized tax benefits were $667
million. If we had recognized all of these benefits, the net impact on our effective tax rate
would have been $530&nbsp;million. There were no material changes due to settlements with tax authorities or the
expiration of the statute of limitations during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007. As a result,
the change in our unrecognized tax benefits during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007 was
insignificant. We expect that the amount of unrecognized tax benefits
will increase by approximately $65-$80&nbsp;million from a variety of
federal, state and foreign tax positions during the next
12&nbsp;months. We include accrued interest and penalties related to uncertain tax positions in our
tax provision. As of January&nbsp;1, 2007, we had $125&nbsp;million of accrued interest and penalties. The
change in accrued interest and penalties during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007 was
insignificant.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We are regularly examined by various federal, state and foreign tax authorities. The U.S. federal
statute of limitations remains open for the year 2000 and onward, with years 2000 through 2003
currently under examination by the IRS. Taxing authorities in various U.S. state and foreign
jurisdictions are currently examining us. U.S. state and foreign jurisdictions have statutes of
limitations generally ranging from 3 to 5&nbsp;years. Years still open to examination by foreign tax
authorities in major jurisdictions include Germany (1999 onward), Brazil (2001 onward), Canada
(2001 onward) and Spain (2001 onward).
</DIV>




<TABLE style="font-size: 10pt" cellspacing="0" border="0" cellpadding="0" width="100%">

<TR style="font-size: 6pt">
<TD colspan="3">&nbsp;</TD>
</TR>

<TR>
<TD width="1%" nowrap valign="top"><B>Item&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;</B></TD>
  <TD width="99%" align="left"><B>Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of Operations.</B></TD>
 </TR>
</TABLE>

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt">
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><U><B>Description of the Company</B></U>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Kraft manufactures and markets packaged food products, including beverages, cheese, snacks,
convenient meals and various packaged grocery products. We manage and report operating results
through two commercial units, Kraft North America and Kraft International. We manage Kraft North
America&#146;s operations by product category, and Kraft International&#146;s operations by geographic
location.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In the first quarter of 2007, Altria Group, Inc. (&#147;Altria&#148;) spun off its entire interest (89.0%) in
Kraft on a pro rata basis to Altria stockholders in a tax-free transaction. Effective as of the
close of business on March&nbsp;30, 2007, all Kraft shares owned by Altria
were distributed to Altria&#146;s stockholders, and our separation from Altria was completed (the
&#147;Distribution&#148;). Before the Distribution, Altria converted its Class&nbsp;B shares of Kraft common
stock into Class&nbsp;A shares of our common stock. The Distribution ratio was calculated by dividing
the number of shares of Kraft Common Stock held by Altria by the number of Altria shares
outstanding on the date of record, March&nbsp;16, 2007. Based on the calculation, the Distribution
ratio was 0.692024 shares of Kraft Common Stock for every share of Altria common stock outstanding.
Following the Distribution, we only have Class&nbsp;A common stock outstanding.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->19<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

results.</I>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B>Acquisitions and Dispositions</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;3, 2007, we announced a binding offer to acquire the global biscuit business of Groupe
Danone S.A. (&#147;Groupe Danone&#148;) for <FONT face="'Times New Roman',times,serif">&#128;</FONT>5.3&nbsp;billion (approximately $7.2&nbsp;billion) in cash. Groupe
Danone&#146;s global biscuit business generated revenues of approximately $2.7&nbsp;billion during 2006. The
transaction is subject to customary closing conditions, including regulatory approval. We expect
it to close by the end of 2007.
</DIV>




<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->20<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In September&nbsp;2006, we acquired the Spanish and Portuguese operations of United Biscuits (&#147;UB&#148;) for
approximately $1.1&nbsp;billion. The non-cash acquisition was financed by our assumption of $541
million of debt issued by the acquired business immediately prior to the acquisition, as well as
$530&nbsp;million of value for the redemption of our outstanding investment in UB, primarily
deep-discount securities. As part of the transaction, we also recovered the rights to all Nabisco
trademarks in the European Union, Eastern Europe, the Middle East and Africa, which UB had held
since 2000. The Spanish and Portuguese operations of UB include its biscuits, dry desserts, canned
meats, tomato and fruit juice businesses. The operations also include seven manufacturing
facilities and 1,300 employees. These businesses contributed net revenues of approximately $118
million during the three months and $215&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the second quarter of 2007, we sold sugar confectionery assets in Romania and related
trademarks. During the first quarter of 2007, we sold our hot cereal assets and trademarks. In
aggregate, we received $203&nbsp;million in proceeds, and recorded pre-tax gains of $20&nbsp;million on these
sales. We recorded an after tax loss of $8&nbsp;million on the hot cereal assets and trademarks sale
due to the differing tax bases.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In 2006, we received $946&nbsp;million in proceeds, and recorded gains of $117&nbsp;million on the following
sales. During the first quarter of 2006, we sold certain Canadian assets and a small U.S. biscuit
brand. We incurred asset impairment charges of $176&nbsp;million in the fourth quarter of 2005 in
recognition of these sales. During the second quarter of 2006, we sold our industrial coconut
assets. During the third quarter of 2006, we sold our pet snacks brand and assets and recorded tax
expense of $57&nbsp;million related to the sale. In addition, we incurred an asset impairment charge of
$86&nbsp;million in the first quarter of 2006 in connection with this sale. During the fourth quarter
of 2006, we sold our rice brand and assets and a U.S. coffee plant.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The aggregate operating results of the businesses sold were not material to our financial
statements in any of the periods presented.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Restructuring Program</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In January&nbsp;2004, we announced a three-year restructuring program (the &#147;Restructuring Program&#148;) and,
in January&nbsp;2006, extended it through 2008. The objectives of this program are to leverage our
global scale, realign and lower our cost structure, and optimize capacity. As part of the
Restructuring Program we anticipate:
</DIV>


<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt">
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 10pt">

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="3%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>incurring approximately $3.0&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges reflecting asset disposals,
severance and implementation costs, including approximately $575&nbsp;million of the charges
during 2007;</TD>
</TR>


<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="3%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>closing up to 40 facilities and eliminating approximately 14,000 positions; and</TD>
</TR>

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="3%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="1%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>using cash to pay for approximately $1.9&nbsp;billion of the $3.0&nbsp;billion in charges.</TD>
</TR>

</TABLE>
</DIV>
<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We incurred charges under the Restructuring Program of $157&nbsp;million during the three months and
$245&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007, and $243&nbsp;million during the three months
and $348&nbsp;million during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2006. In total, we have incurred $1.9
billion in charges since the inception of the Restructuring Program. We expect to pay cash for
approximately 60% of the charges. In connection with severance programs announced since 2004, we
expect to eliminate approximately 10,500 positions. As of June&nbsp;30, 2007, we had eliminated
approximately 9,800 of these positions.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition, we expect to spend approximately $550&nbsp;million in capital to implement the
Restructuring Program. We have spent $300&nbsp;million in capital since the inception of the
Restructuring Program, including $55&nbsp;million spent in the first six months of 2007. Cumulative
annualized cost savings resulting from the Restructuring Program were approximately $540&nbsp;million
through 2006. Cost savings totaled approximately $120&nbsp;million in the first six months of 2007,
resulting in cumulative annualized savings under the Restructuring Program of approximately $660
million to date. We expect these
savings to reach approximately $725&nbsp;million by the end of 2007. Refer to Note 2, <I>Asset Impairment,
Exit and Implementation Costs</I>, for further details of our Restructuring Program.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Asset Impairment Charges</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the first quarter of 2007, we completed our annual review of goodwill and intangible assets.
No impairments resulted from this review. During the first quarter of 2006, we completed our
annual review of goodwill and intangible assets and recorded a $24&nbsp;million non-cash charge for
impairment of biscuits assets in Egypt and hot cereal assets in the U.S. We recorded these charges
as asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->21<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">During the first quarter of 2007, we sold our hot cereal assets and trademarks for a pre-tax gain
of $12&nbsp;million. We previously incurred an asset impairment charge of $69&nbsp;million in the fourth
quarter of 2006 in connection with this sale. The charge included the write-off of a portion of
the associated goodwill, intangible assets and property, plant and equipment. We recorded the
charge as asset impairment and exit costs on the 2006 consolidated statement of earnings, and no
further charges were incurred in 2007. In the first quarter of 2006, we incurred an asset
impairment charge of $86&nbsp;million in anticipation of the pet snacks brand and assets sale. The
charge included the write-off of a portion of the associated goodwill, intangible assets and
property, plant and equipment. We recorded aggregate asset impairment charges in the
first quarter of 2006 amounting to $110&nbsp;million or $0.05 per diluted share.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Provision for Income Taxes</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our tax rate was 32.0% in the second quarter of 2007 and 32.8% in the first six months of 2007.
Our provision for income taxes includes a net benefit of $19&nbsp;million in the second quarter of 2007
primarily resulting from the resolution of outstanding items in our international operations and
various state jurisdictions. For the first six months of 2007, the provision includes a net tax
benefit of $8&nbsp;million primarily resulting from the second quarter resolutions, partially offset by
tax costs associated with the sale of our hot cereal assets and trademarks.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As discussed in Note 14, <I>Income Taxes</I>, Altria transferred our federal tax contingencies of $375
million to our balance sheet and related interest income of $77&nbsp;million at the end of the first
quarter of 2007, as a result of the Distribution (or $0.03 per diluted share). Following the
Distribution, we are no longer a member of the Altria consolidated tax return group, and we will
file our own federal consolidated income tax return. As a result of filing separately, we
currently estimate the annual amount of lost tax benefits to be in the range of $50&nbsp;million to $75
million.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In the first quarter of 2006, the IRS concluded its examination of Altria&#146;s consolidated tax
returns for the years 1996 through 1999. The IRS issued a final Revenue Agents Report on March&nbsp;15,
2006. Consequently, Altria reimbursed us $337&nbsp;million for federal tax reserves that were no longer
necessary and $46&nbsp;million for interest ($29&nbsp;million net of tax). We also recognized net state tax
reversals of $39&nbsp;million, for a total tax provision benefit of $376&nbsp;million ($337&nbsp;million federal
plus $39&nbsp;million state). The total benefit to net earnings that we recognized in the first quarter
of 2006 due to the IRS settlement was $405&nbsp;million, or $0.24 per diluted share.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Consolidated Results of Operations</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">The following discussion compares our consolidated results of operations for the three months ended
June&nbsp;30, 2007 and 2006, as well as the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007 and 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Many factors impact the timing of sales to our customers. These factors include, among others, the
timing of holidays and other annual or special events, seasonality, significant weather conditions,
timing of our own or customer incentive programs and pricing actions, customer inventory programs,
our initiatives to improve supply chain efficiency, the financial condition of our customers and
general economic conditions. For instance, changes in the timing of the Easter holiday will often
affect first and second quarter comparisons with the prior year.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Net Revenues </I>- Net revenues increased $586&nbsp;million (6.8%), due to favorable mix (3.1 pp), favorable
currency (2.2 pp), higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending (1.7 pp) and the impact of
acquisitions (1.4 pp), partially offset by the impact of divestitures (0.9 pp) and lower volume
(0.7 pp). Currency movements increased net revenues by $190&nbsp;million due primarily to the
continuing weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro. Total volume decreased 0.2%, resulting
from declines in all North American segments due primarily to the impact of divestitures and
declines in ready to drink beverages, partially offset by higher shipments in European Union and
Developing Markets.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Operating Income </I>- Operating income increased $12&nbsp;million (1.0%), due primarily to favorable
volume/mix ($93&nbsp;million), and lower Restructuring Program charges ($86&nbsp;million), partially offset
by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($138&nbsp;million, including higher marketing
support), and higher total manufacturing costs, including higher commodity costs, net of the impact
of higher pricing ($43&nbsp;million). Currency movements increased operating income by $17&nbsp;million due
primarily to the continuing weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Net Earnings </I>- Net earnings of $707&nbsp;million increased by $25&nbsp;million (3.7%) driven by a favorable
tax rate and operating income increases.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Earnings per Share </I>- Second quarter 2007 diluted earnings per share were $0.44, up 7.3% from $0.41
in 2006. During second quarter 2007, we incurred $0.06 per diluted share ($157&nbsp;million before
taxes) in Restructuring Program costs as compared to $0.10 per diluted share ($243&nbsp;million before
taxes) in the second quarter of 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt"><I>Net Revenues </I>- Net revenues increased $1,049&nbsp;million (6.3%), due primarily to favorable mix (2.7
pp), favorable currency (2.1 pp), the impact of acquisitions (1.3 pp) and higher pricing, net of
increased promotional spending (1.0 pp), partially offset by the impact of divestitures (1.0 pp).
Currency movements increased net revenues by $362&nbsp;million due primarily to
the continuing weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro. Total volume increased 0.3%, driven
by higher shipments in the European Union and Developing Markets, partially offset by lower volume
in all North American segments due primarily to the impact of divestitures and declines in ready to
drink beverages.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Operating Income </I>- Operating income increased $117&nbsp;million (5.3%), due primarily to favorable
volume/mix ($210&nbsp;million), 2006 asset impairment charges related to the divested pet snacks and hot
cereal assets and trademarks and biscuits assets in Egypt ($110&nbsp;million), and lower Restructuring
Program charges ($103&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research
costs ($257&nbsp;million, including higher marketing support), and higher total manufacturing costs,
including higher commodity costs, net of the impact of higher pricing ($77&nbsp;million). Currency
movements increased operating income by $39&nbsp;million due primarily to the continuing weakness of the
U.S. dollar against the euro.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Net Earnings </I>- Net earnings of $1,409&nbsp;million decreased by $279&nbsp;million (16.5%) primarily due to a
favorable tax rate in 2006 from a significant tax resolution.
</DIV>


<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->23<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Earnings per Share </I>- In the first six months of 2007 diluted earnings per share were $0.87, down
14.7% from $1.02 in 2006. During the first six months of 2007, we incurred $0.10 per diluted share
($245&nbsp;million before taxes) in Restructuring Program costs as compared to $0.14 per diluted share
($348&nbsp;million before taxes) in the first six months of 2006. Due to the Distribution, we
recognized interest income of $0.03 per diluted share ($77&nbsp;million before taxes) from tax reserve
transfers from Altria. In the first quarter of 2006, we benefited from favorable federal and state
tax resolutions amounting to $405&nbsp;million, or $0.24 per diluted share. Additionally, we recorded
asset impairment charges in the first quarter of 2006 amounting to $110&nbsp;million or $0.05 per
diluted share.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Results of Operations by Business Segment</B>

three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007 and 2006, and also compares the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2007 and
2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">As discussed in Note 11, <I>Segment Reporting</I>, our management uses segment operating income to
evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Segment operating income excludes unallocated
general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles. Management believes it is appropriate
to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Refer to Note
2, <I>Asset Impairment, Exit and Implementation Costs</I>, for a breakout of charges by segment.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues increased $35&nbsp;million (4.3%), due to favorable mix (8.9 pp) and higher net pricing
(1.0 pp), partially offset by lower volume (5.6 pp). Favorable mix was driven by <I>Crystal Light On
the Go </I>base growth and new products, and growth in premium coffee. Higher commodity related
pricing in coffee was partially offset by higher promotional spending. Net revenues growth in the
quarter was partially offset by ongoing weakness in ready-to-drink beverages and lower shipments of
<I>Maxwell House </I>coffee.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $19&nbsp;million (16.5%) due primarily to favorable mix, partially
offset by higher commodity costs (primarily coffee and packaging).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt">Net revenues increased $66&nbsp;million (4.1%), due to favorable mix (6.5 pp) and higher net pricing
(0.5 pp), which was partially offset by lower volume (2.9 pp). Favorable mix from <I>Crystal Light On
the Go </I>sticks and premium coffee drove higher net revenues. Higher commodity based pricing in
coffee was partially offset by increased promotional spending in ready-to-drink beverages. Net
revenues growth was tempered by lower shipments of <I>Maxwell House </I>coffee and ready-to-drink
beverages.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $11&nbsp;million (4.2%), due primarily to favorable mix, partially
offset by higher commodity costs (primarily coffee and packaging).
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $45&nbsp;million (3.0%) due primarily to higher commodity based pricing (4.4 pp)
and favorable mix
(0.7 pp), partially offset by lower volume (1.8 pp). Cheese net revenues increased, driven by
commodity based pricing and favorable mix from new product introductions, partially offset by lower
shipments. In foodservice, net revenues growth from commodity based pricing was partially offset
by lower volume due to the discontinuation of lower margin product lines and unfavorable mix.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $30&nbsp;million (16.8%), as the favorable impact of pricing was more
than offset by higher commodity costs, higher marketing, administration and research costs
(including higher marketing support) and higher implementation costs related to the Restructuring
Program. The change was partially offset by lower Restructuring Program charges and a 2006 loss on
the sale of industrial coconut assets.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $44&nbsp;million (1.5%), due primarily to higher commodity based net pricing (2.6
pp) and favorable mix (0.5 pp), offset by lower volume (1.2 pp). Cheese net revenues increased
driven by higher pricing and favorable volume and mix. In foodservice, net revenues declined due
to the discontinuation of lower margin product lines and unfavorable mix, partially offset by
higher commodity based net pricing.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $40&nbsp;million (10.5%) due primarily to higher marketing,
administration and research costs (including higher marketing support).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $44&nbsp;million (3.6%), due to favorable mix (3.4 pp), higher net pricing (1.2
pp) and higher volume (0.7 pp), partially offset by the impact of the
divested rice brand and assets (1.7
pp). Favorable product mix and higher volume from new product introductions including <I>Oscar Mayer
Deli Creations </I>and <I>DiGiorno Ultimate </I>pizza and the continued success of <I>Oscar Mayer Deli Shaved</I>
sandwich meat and <I>California Pizza Kitchen </I>pizza drove higher net revenues. Higher volume from new
products was partially offset by lower shipments of chicken strips due to a first quarter recall.
Meat net revenues also grew driven by higher commodity based net pricing, primarily in bacon.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $27&nbsp;million (14.6%) as gains from higher pricing and lower
Restructuring Program charges were more than offset by higher commodity costs, higher marketing,
administration and research costs and the impact of divestitures.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->26<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $76&nbsp;million (3.1%), due to favorable mix (2.9 pp), higher volume (1.3 pp)
and higher net pricing (0.8 pp), offset by the impact of divestitures (1.9 pp). Net revenues
increased in meat due to higher shipments of sandwich meat, new product introductions, favorable
mix and higher commodity based net pricing, partially offset by lower shipments of chicken strips
due to a first quarter recall. In pizza, net revenues increased due to the introduction of
<I>DiGiorno Ultimate </I>and
higher shipments of <I>California Pizza Kitchen </I>products. Macaroni and cheese net revenues also
increased due to higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending, and favorable mix.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $44&nbsp;million (11.4%), as gains from higher pricing and lower
Restructuring Program charges were more than offset by higher commodity costs, higher marketing,
administration and research costs and the impact of divestitures.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues decreased $14&nbsp;million (1.8%), due primarily to lower volume (2.3 pp), partially offset
by higher net pricing (0.6 pp). Net revenues declined due to lower shipments in spoonable and
pourable salad dressings and dry packaged desserts, partially offset by higher net pricing in
spoonables and dry packaged desserts.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $27&nbsp;million (9.2%), due primarily to unfavorable volume/mix.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues decreased $23&nbsp;million (1.6%), due primarily to lower volume (1.5 pp) and the impact of
divestitures (0.5 pp), partially offset by higher net pricing (0.8 pp). The impact of lower
shipments in barbeque sauce and spoonable and pourable salad dressings was partially offset by
higher net pricing in spoonable salad dressings and dry packaged desserts.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $31&nbsp;million (6.2%), due primarily to unfavorable volume/mix and
higher marketing, administration and research costs.
</DIV>




<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->27<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $7&nbsp;million (0.4%), due primarily to favorable mix (2.6 pp) and higher volume
(0.8 pp), partially offset by the impact of the pet snack and hot cereal divestitures (3.3 pp).
Biscuit net revenues increased, driven by favorable mix in cookies. Net revenues growth in bars
was driven by higher volume due to the introduction of <I>Nabisco </I>100 Calorie Packs and <I>Back to Nature</I>
bars.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income decreased $3&nbsp;million (1.1%), due primarily to higher marketing,
administration and research costs (including higher marketing support) and the impact of
divestitures, partially offset by favorable volume/mix and lower manufacturing costs (productivity,
partially offset by higher commodities).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $13&nbsp;million (0.4%), due primarily to favorable mix (2.4 pp) and higher
volume (1.8 pp), partially offset by the impact of divestitures (3.5 pp). Favorable mix and higher
shipments in cookies and crackers due to new product introductions drove higher net revenues. Bar
net revenues increased due to new product introductions and continued success of <I>South Beach Diet</I>
bars.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $103&nbsp;million (25.1%), due primarily to a 2006 asset impairment
charge related to the divested pet snacks and hot cereal assets and trademarks, favorable
volume/mix and lower manufacturing costs. Higher marketing, administration and research costs
(including higher marketing support) and the impact of divestitures, partially offset the segment
operating income favorability.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $302&nbsp;million (19.6%), due to favorable currency (10.2 pp), the impact of the
UB acquisition (7.4 pp), higher volume (1.8 pp) and favorable mix (1.6 pp), partially offset by
lower net pricing (1.4 pp). Net revenues increased, driven by volume growth and favorable mix in
coffee and chocolate due to new product introductions and higher marketing support. Lower net
pricing reflects higher spending to promote premium chocolate products and to counter price based
competition in mainstream coffee in Germany.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $39&nbsp;million (45.3%), due primarily to lower Restructuring
Program charges, favorable volume/mix, lower fixed manufacturing costs, favorable currency and the
impact of the UB acquisition. Offsetting these favorabilities were higher marketing,
administration and research costs (including an $18&nbsp;million gain on sale of a manufacturing plant
in 2006), higher commodity costs, lower net pricing and higher implementation costs associated with
the Restructuring Program.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $585&nbsp;million (19.5%), due to favorable currency (10.1 pp), the impact of the
UB acquisition (7.0 pp), higher volume (2.4 pp) and favorable mix (1.7 pp), partially offset by
lower net pricing (1.7 pp). Volume related growth and favorable mix was driven by premium
chocolate, due to new product introductions and promotional activities, and higher shipments in
mainstream coffee. Lower net pricing reflects higher promotional spending in chocolate and cheese,
and feature pricing in coffee in Germany.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $28&nbsp;million (13.0%) as favorable volume/mix, higher net pricing,
favorable currency, the impact of the UB acquisition, lower fixed manufacturing costs, lower
Restructuring Program charges and a 2006 asset impairment charge related to the divested biscuits
assets in Egypt more than offset higher marketing, administration and research costs, higher
commodity costs and higher implementation costs associated with the Restructuring Program.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->29<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $167&nbsp;million (14.7%), due primarily to higher net pricing (5.8 pp), higher
volume (3.7 pp), favorable currency (2.9 pp) and favorable mix (2.0 pp). In Eastern Europe, Middle
East &#038; Africa, net revenues increased, driven by growth in coffee and chocolate and pricing in
Russia, Romania and Ukraine. Latin American net revenues increased, driven by favorable mix and
pricing in Brazil, favorable volume/mix and higher pricing in Argentina and higher pricing in
Venezuela. In Asia Pacific, net revenues increased, primarily due to currency.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $38&nbsp;million (38.8%), due primarily to the contribution of higher
pricing, favorable volume/mix, lower Restructuring Program costs and a gain on the sale of sugar
confectionery assets in Romania and related trademarks, partially offset by higher marketing,
administration and research costs (including higher marketing support) and higher input costs.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Net revenues increased $288&nbsp;million (13.4%), due primarily to higher net pricing (4.7 pp),
favorable currency (3.0pp), higher volume (2.8 pp) and favorable mix (2.7 pp). In Eastern Europe,
Middle East &#038; Africa, net revenues increased due to growth in coffee and chocolate in Russia,
Romania and Ukraine. Latin American net revenues increased due to higher pricing and favorable
volume and mix, particularly in Brazil, Venezuela and Argentina. In Asia Pacific, net revenues
increased, due primarily to currency.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Segment operating income increased $96&nbsp;million (72.2%) due primarily to lower Restructuring Program
costs, favorable volume/mix and the contribution of higher pricing, partially offset by higher
marketing, administration and research costs and higher input costs.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Liquidity</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Net Cash Provided by Operating Activities:</I></DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">During the first six months of 2007, operating activities provided $1,410&nbsp;million net cash,
compared with $1,606&nbsp;million in the comparable 2006 period. Operating cash flows decreased in the
first six months of 2007 in comparison with the same period in 2006 primarily because of the
previously discussed tax reimbursement from Altria in 2006 related to the closure of a tax audit
and higher working capital, primarily inventories, due to increased commodity costs. The decrease
in operating cash flows was partially offset by the previously discussed tax transfer from Altria
upon the Distribution.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Net Cash Used in Investing Activities:</I></DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">During the first six months of 2007, net cash used in investing activities was $293&nbsp;million,
compared with $296&nbsp;million in the first six months of 2006. The slight decrease in cash used in
investing activities primarily relates to higher proceeds from the sales of businesses, partially
offset by higher capital expenditures in 2007. During the first six months of 2007, we sold sugar
confectionery assets in Romania and related trademarks, as well as hot cereal assets and
trademarks. During the first six months of 2006, we sold our industrial coconut assets, certain
Canadian assets and a small U.S. biscuit brand.
</DIV>




<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->30<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>



<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Capital expenditures for the first six months of 2007 were $506&nbsp;million, compared with $450&nbsp;million
in the first six months of 2006. We expect full-year capital expenditures to be flat to 2006
expenditures of $1.2&nbsp;billion, including capital expenditures required for the Restructuring Program
and systems investments. We expect to fund these expenditures from operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Net Cash Used in Financing Activities:</I></DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">During the first six months of 2007, we used $950&nbsp;million net cash in financing activities,
compared with $1,249&nbsp;million that we used during the first six months of 2006. The decrease in net
cash used in financing activities is due primarily to the issuance of new commercial paper,
partially offset by an increase in our Common Stock share repurchases and the repayment of
long-term debt that matured in the first six months of 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Debt:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Our total debt was $12.5&nbsp;billion at June&nbsp;30, 2007, and $10.8&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2006. Our
total debt balance at December&nbsp;31, 2006, included amounts due to Altria and affiliates. Our
debt-to-capitalization ratio was 0.31 at June&nbsp;30, 2007, and 0.27 at December&nbsp;31, 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In June&nbsp;2007, $1.0&nbsp;billion of our long-term debt matured. In July&nbsp;2007, an additional $400&nbsp;million
of our long-term debt matured. We repaid the debt with the proceeds from the issuance of
commercial paper.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">We had short-term amounts payable to Altria and affiliates of $5&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2007 and $607
million at December&nbsp;31, 2006, which included $364&nbsp;million of accrued dividends. Current amounts
due to Altria reflect fees for transition services. Prior to the Distribution, the amounts payable
to Altria generally included accrued dividends, taxes and service fees.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Credit Ratings:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">Subsequent to the announcement of our binding offer to acquire the global biscuit business of
Groupe Danone, Standard &#038; Poor&#146;s affirmed our short-term credit rating of A-1 and our long-term
debt rating of A-, and revised the outlook from stable to negative. Moody&#146;s downgraded our
long-term credit rating from Baa1 to Baa2 with stable outlook and affirmed our short-term credit
rating of P-2. Fitch downgraded the long-term credit rating from A-
to BBB&#043;, with a negative outlook, and affirmed the short-term credit rating at F2.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Credit Lines:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">We maintain revolving credit facilities that we have historically used for general corporate
purposes and to support our commercial paper issuances. We have a $4.5&nbsp;billion, multi-year
revolving credit facility that expires in April&nbsp;2010. On May&nbsp;24, 2007, we entered into a $1.5
billion, 364-day revolving credit agreement. No amounts were drawn on either of these facilities
at June&nbsp;30, 2007.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">On July&nbsp;2, 2007, we entered into a commitment letter in connection with a proposed senior unsecured
364-day bridge facility for <FONT face="'Times New Roman',times,serif">&#128;</FONT>5.3&nbsp;billion (approximately $7.2&nbsp;billion). We plan to use the
facility to finance the Groupe Danone biscuit business acquisition. We intend to repay borrowings
under this facility from proceeds of the issuance of investment grade bonds or other securities.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Our revolving credit facilities require us to maintain a net worth of at least $20.0&nbsp;billion. At
June&nbsp;30, 2007, we had a $27.5&nbsp;billion net worth. We expect to continue to meet this covenant. The
revolving credit facilities have no other financial covenants, credit rating triggers or provisions
that could require us to post collateral as security. We refinance long-term and short-term debt
from time to time. The nature and amount of our long-term and short-term debt and the
proportionate amount of each varies as a result of future business requirements, market conditions
and other factors.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition to the above, some of our international subsidiaries maintain primarily uncommitted
credit lines to meet short-term working capital needs. These credit lines amounted to
approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion at June&nbsp;30, 2007. At June&nbsp;30, 2007, borrowings on these lines amounted
to approximately $520&nbsp;million.
</DIV>



<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><!-- Folio -->31<!-- /Folio -->
</DIV>

<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>




<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><I>Guarantees:</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 0pt">As discussed in Note 8, <I>Contingencies</I>, at June&nbsp;30, 2007, we have third-party guarantees because of
our acquisition, divestiture and construction activities. As part of those transactions, we
guarantee that third parties will make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. At
June&nbsp;30, 2007, our third-party guarantees were approximately $27&nbsp;million, of which approximately $7
million have no specified expiration dates. Substantially all of the remainder expire at various
times through 2016. We have a liability of $21&nbsp;million on our condensed consolidated balance sheet
at June&nbsp;30, 2007, relating to these guarantees.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">In addition, at June&nbsp;30, 2007, we were contingently liable for $235&nbsp;million of guarantees related
to our own performance. These include surety bonds related to dairy commodity purchases and
guarantees related to the payment of custom duties and taxes, and letters of credit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">Guarantees do not have, and we do not expect them to have a significant impact on our liquidity.
We believe that our cash from operations and our existing credit facilities will provide sufficient
liquidity to meet our working capital needs (including the cash requirements of the Restructuring
Program), planned capital expenditures, future contractual obligations and payment of our
anticipated quarterly dividends.
</DIV>
